//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Wisoff_on_the_Arm_-_GPN-2000-001069.jpg/600px-Wisoff_on_the_Arm_-_GPN-2000-001069.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Inside a space suit on a robotic arm, 1993\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Human spaceflight\n       </b>\n       (also referred to as\n       <b>\n        manned spaceflight\n       </b>\n       ) is\n       <a href="/wiki/Spaceflight" title="Spaceflight">\n        space travel\n       </a>\n       with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">\n        crew\n       </a>\n       or passengers aboard the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">\n        spacecraft\n       </a>\n       . Spacecraft carrying people may be operated directly, by human crew, or it may be either\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telerobotic" title="Telerobotic">\n        remotely operated\n       </a>\n       from ground stations on Earth or be\n       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_robot" title="Autonomous robot">\n        autonomous\n       </a>\n       , able to carry out a specific mission with no human involvement.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">\n        first human spaceflight\n       </a>\n       was launched by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">\n        Soviet Union\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmonautics_Day" title="Cosmonautics Day">\n        12 April 1961\n       </a>\n       as a part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vostok_program" title="Vostok program">\n        Vostok program\n       </a>\n       , with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmonaut" title="Cosmonaut">\n        cosmonaut\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">\n        Yuri Gagarin\n       </a>\n       aboard. Humans have been continuously present in space for\n       <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n        7003621500000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n       </span>\n       17\xc2\xa0years and 6\xc2\xa0days on the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       . All early human spaceflight was crewed, where at least some of the passengers acted to carry out tasks of piloting or operating the spacecraft. After 2015, several human-capable spacecraft are being explicitly designed with the ability to operate autonomously.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since the retirement of the US\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       in 2011, only\n       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">\n        Russia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">\n        China\n       </a>\n       have maintained human spaceflight capability with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_program" title="Soyuz program">\n        Soyuz program\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_program" title="Shenzhou program">\n        Shenzhou program\n       </a>\n       . Currently, all expeditions to the International Space Station use\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_(spacecraft)" title="Soyuz (spacecraft)">\n        Soyuz\n       </a>\n       vehicles, which remain attached to the station to allow quick return if needed. The United States is developing commercial crew transportation to facilitate domestic access to ISS and low Earth orbit, as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n        Orion\n       </a>\n       vehicle for beyond-low Earth orbit applications.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While spaceflight has typically been a government-directed activity, commercial spaceflight has gradually been taking on a greater role. The first private human spaceflight took place on 21 June 2004, when\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceShipOne" title="SpaceShipOne">\n        SpaceShipOne\n       </a>\n       conducted a suborbital flight, and a\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_private_spaceflight_companies" title="List of private spaceflight companies">\n        number of non-governmental companies\n       </a>\n       have been working to develop a\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">\n        space tourism\n       </a>\n       industry. NASA has also played a role to stimulate\n       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">\n        private spaceflight\n       </a>\n       through programs such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </a>\n       (COTS) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        Commercial Crew Development\n       </a>\n       (CCDev). With its 2011 budget proposals released in 2010,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the Obama administration moved towards a model where commercial companies would supply NASA with transportation services of both people and cargo transport to low Earth orbit. The vehicles used for these services could then serve both NASA and potential commercial customers. Commercial resupply of ISS began two years after the retirement of the Shuttle, and commercial crew launches could begin by 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n class="tocnumber">\n               5.1.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Life support\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16">\n             <a href="#Medical_issues">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.1.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Medical issues\n              </span>\n             </a>\n             <ul>\n              <li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-17">\n               <a href="#Microgravity">\n                <span class="tocnumber">\n                 5.1.2.1\n                </span>\n                <span class="toctext">\n                 Microgravity\n                </span>\n               </a>\n              </li>\n              <li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-18">\n               <a href="#Radiation">\n                <span class="tocnumber">\n                 5.1.2.2\n                </span>\n                <span class="toctext">\n                 Radiation\n                </span>\n               </a>\n              </li>\n              <li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-19">\n               <a href="#Isolation">\n                <span class="tocnumber">\n                 5.1.2.3\n                </span>\n                <span class="toctext">\n                 Isolation\n                </span>\n               </a>\n              </li>\n             </ul>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20">\n           <a href="#Mechanical_hazards">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Mechanical hazards\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21">\n             <a href="#Launch">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.2.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Launch\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22">\n             <a href="#Reentry_and_landing">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.2.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Reentry and landing\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23">\n             <a href="#Artificial_atmosphere">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.2.3\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Artificial atmosphere\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-24">\n             <a href="#Reliability">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.2.4\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Reliability\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a href="#Fatality_risk">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Fatality risk\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28">\n           <a href="#Citations">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Citations\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29">\n           <a href="#Bibliography">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Bibliography\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_spaceflight" title="History of spaceflight">\n        History of spaceflight\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_era">\n        Cold War era\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cold War era">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">\n        Space Race\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vostok_Spacecraft_Diagram.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="362" data-file-width="512" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Vostok_Spacecraft_Diagram.svg/220px-Vostok_Spacecraft_Diagram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Vostok_Spacecraft_Diagram.svg/330px-Vostok_Spacecraft_Diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Vostok_Spacecraft_Diagram.svg/440px-Vostok_Spacecraft_Diagram.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vostok_Spacecraft_Diagram.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Vostok space capsule, which carried the first human into orbit\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mercury_Friendship7_Bassett_Celestia.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1440" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Mercury_Friendship7_Bassett_Celestia.jpg/220px-Mercury_Friendship7_Bassett_Celestia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Mercury_Friendship7_Bassett_Celestia.jpg/330px-Mercury_Friendship7_Bassett_Celestia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Mercury_Friendship7_Bassett_Celestia.jpg/440px-Mercury_Friendship7_Bassett_Celestia.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mercury_Friendship7_Bassett_Celestia.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Mercury capsule, which carried the first Americans into space\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:As11-40-5886.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="738" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/As11-40-5886.jpg/220px-As11-40-5886.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/As11-40-5886.jpg/330px-As11-40-5886.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/As11-40-5886.jpg/440px-As11-40-5886.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:As11-40-5886.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">\n          Neil Armstrong\n         </a>\n         became the first human to land and walk on the Moon, July 1969.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Human spaceflight capability was first developed during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">\n        Cold War\n       </a>\n       between the United States and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">\n        Soviet Union\n       </a>\n       (USSR), which developed the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile" title="Intercontinental ballistic missile">\n        intercontinental ballistic missile\n       </a>\n       rockets to deliver\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">\n        nuclear weapons\n       </a>\n       . These rockets were large enough to be adapted to carry the first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artificial_satellite" title="Artificial satellite">\n        artificial satellites\n       </a>\n       into\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       . After the first satellites were launched in 1957 and 1958, the US worked on\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Mercury" title="Project Mercury">\n        Project Mercury\n       </a>\n       to launch men singly into orbit, while the USSR secretly pursued the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_programme" title="Vostok programme">\n        Vostok program\n       </a>\n       to accomplish the same thing. The USSR launched the first human in space,\n       <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">\n        Yuri Gagarin\n       </a>\n       , into a single orbit in\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">\n        Vostok 1\n       </a>\n       on a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vostok_3KA" title="Vostok 3KA">\n        Vostok 3KA\n       </a>\n       rocket, on 12 April 1961. The US launched its first\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">\n        astronaut\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shepard" title="Alan Shepard">\n        Alan Shepard\n       </a>\n       , on a suborbital flight aboard\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_7" title="Freedom 7">\n         Freedom 7\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Mercury-Redstone_Launch_Vehicle" title="Mercury-Redstone Launch Vehicle">\n        Mercury-Redstone rocket\n       </a>\n       , on 5 May 1961. Unlike Gagarin, Shepard manually\n       <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">\n        controlled his spacecraft\'s attitude\n       </a>\n       , and landed inside it. The first American in orbit was\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Glenn" title="John Glenn">\n        John Glenn\n       </a>\n       aboard\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friendship_7" title="Friendship 7">\n         Friendship 7\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , launched 20 February 1962 on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlas_LV-3B" title="Atlas LV-3B">\n        Mercury-Atlas rocket\n       </a>\n       . The USSR launched five more cosmonauts in Vostok\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_capsule" title="Space capsule">\n        capsules\n       </a>\n       , including the first woman in space,\n       <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Tereshkova" title="Valentina Tereshkova">\n        Valentina Tereshkova\n       </a>\n       aboard\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_6" title="Vostok 6">\n        Vostok 6\n       </a>\n       on 16 June 1963. The US launched a total of two astronauts in suborbital flight and four into orbit through 1963.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       US President\n       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">\n        John F. Kennedy\n       </a>\n       raised the stakes of the Space Race by setting the goal of landing a man on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n        Moon\n       </a>\n       and returning him safely by the end of the 1960s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The US started the three-man\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo program\n       </a>\n       in 1961 to accomplish this, launched by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_(rocket_family)" title="Saturn (rocket family)">\n        Saturn family of launch vehicles\n       </a>\n       , and the interim two-man\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Gemini" title="Project Gemini">\n        Project Gemini\n       </a>\n       in 1962, which flew 10 missions launched by\n       <a href="/wiki/Titan_II_GLV" title="Titan II GLV">\n        Titan II rockets\n       </a>\n       in 1965 and 1966. Gemini\'s objective was to support Apollo by developing American orbital spaceflight experience and techniques to be used in the Moon mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Meanwhile, the USSR remained silent about their intentions to send humans to the Moon, and proceeded to stretch the limits of their single-pilot Vostok capsule into a two- or three-person\n       <a href="/wiki/Voskhod_programme" title="Voskhod programme">\n        Voskhod\n       </a>\n       capsule to compete with Gemini. They were able to launch two orbital flights in 1964 and 1965 and achieved the first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacewalk" title="Spacewalk">\n        spacewalk\n       </a>\n       , made by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexei_Leonov" title="Alexei Leonov">\n        Alexei Leonov\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Voskhod_2" title="Voskhod 2">\n        Voskhod 2\n       </a>\n       on 8 March 1965. But Voskhod did not have Gemini\'s capability to maneuver in orbit, and the program was terminated. The US Gemini flights did not accomplish the first spacewalk, but overcame the early Soviet lead by performing several spacewalks and solving the problem of astronaut fatigue caused by overcoming the lack of gravity, demonstrating up to two weeks endurance in a human spaceflight, and the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_rendezvous" title="Space rendezvous">\n        space rendezvous\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Docking_and_berthing_of_spacecraft" title="Docking and berthing of spacecraft">\n        dockings\n       </a>\n       of spacecraft.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The US succeeded in developing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n        Saturn V\n       </a>\n       rocket necessary to send the Apollo spacecraft to the Moon, and sent\n       <a href="/wiki/Frank_Borman" title="Frank Borman">\n        Frank Borman\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Lovell" title="Jim Lovell">\n        James Lovell\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Anders" title="William Anders">\n        William Anders\n       </a>\n       into 10 orbits around the Moon in\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">\n        Apollo 8\n       </a>\n       in December 1968. In July 1969,\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">\n        Apollo 11\n       </a>\n       accomplished Kennedy\'s goal by landing\n       <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">\n        Neil Armstrong\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">\n        Buzz Aldrin\n       </a>\n       on the Moon 21 July and returning them safely on 24 July along with Command Module pilot\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Collins_(astronaut)" title="Michael Collins (astronaut)">\n        Michael Collins\n       </a>\n       . A total of six Apollo missions landed 12 men to walk on the Moon through 1972, half of which drove\n       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Roving_Vehicle" title="Lunar Roving Vehicle">\n        electric powered vehicles\n       </a>\n       on the surface. The crew of\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">\n        Apollo 13\n       </a>\n       , Lovell,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jack_Swigert" title="Jack Swigert">\n        Jack Swigert\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fred_Haise" title="Fred Haise">\n        Fred Haise\n       </a>\n       , survived a catastrophic in-flight spacecraft failure and returned to Earth safely without landing on the Moon.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soyuz_7K-OK(A)_drawing.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="225" data-file-width="400" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Soyuz_7K-OK%28A%29_drawing.svg/220px-Soyuz_7K-OK%28A%29_drawing.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Soyuz_7K-OK%28A%29_drawing.svg/330px-Soyuz_7K-OK%28A%29_drawing.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Soyuz_7K-OK%28A%29_drawing.svg/440px-Soyuz_7K-OK%28A%29_drawing.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soyuz_7K-OK(A)_drawing.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Soyuz 7K-OK spacecraft, 1967\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Meanwhile, the USSR secretly pursued\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_manned_lunar_programs" title="Soviet manned lunar programs">\n        human lunar orbiting and landing programs\n       </a>\n       . They successfully developed the three-person\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">\n        Soyuz spacecraft\n       </a>\n       for use in the lunar programs, but failed to develop the\n       <a href="/wiki/N1_(rocket)" title="N1 (rocket)">\n        N1 rocket\n       </a>\n       necessary for a human landing, and discontinued the lunar programs in 1974.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On losing the Moon race, they concentrated on the development of\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">\n        space stations\n       </a>\n       , using the Soyuz as a ferry to take cosmonauts to and from the stations. They started with a series of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salyut_program" title="Salyut program">\n        Salyut\n       </a>\n       sortie stations from 1971 to 1986.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After the Apollo program, the US launched the\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       sortie space station in 1973, manning it for 171 days with three crews aboard Apollo spacecraft. President\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">\n        Richard Nixon\n       </a>\n       and Soviet Premier\n       <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">\n        Leonid Brezhnev\n       </a>\n       negotiated an easing of relations known as\n       <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="D\xc3\xa9tente">\n        d\xc3\xa9tente\n       </a>\n       , an easing of Cold War tensions. As part of this, they negotiated the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Apollo-Soyuz Test Project">\n        Apollo-Soyuz Test Project\n       </a>\n       , in which an Apollo spacecraft carrying a special docking adapter module rendezvoused and docked with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_19" title="Soyuz 19">\n        Soyuz 19\n       </a>\n       in 1975. The American and Russian crews shook hands in space, but the purpose of the flight was purely diplomatic and symbolic.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_American_Rockwell_P333.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="222" data-file-width="342" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/North_American_Rockwell_P333.jpg/220px-North_American_Rockwell_P333.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/North_American_Rockwell_P333.jpg/330px-North_American_Rockwell_P333.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2f/North_American_Rockwell_P333.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:North_American_Rockwell_P333.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle as originally designed by North American Rockwell, 1969\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Nixon appointed his Vice President\n       <a href="/wiki/Spiro_Agnew" title="Spiro Agnew">\n        Spiro Agnew\n       </a>\n       to head a Space Task Group in 1969 to recommend follow-on human spaceflight programs after Apollo. The group proposed an ambitious\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Transportation_System" title="Space Transportation System">\n        Space Transportation System\n       </a>\n       based on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_design_process" title="Space Shuttle design process">\n        reusable Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       which consisted of a winged, internally fueled orbiter stage burning liquid hydrogen, launched by a similar, but larger\n       <a href="/wiki/RP-1" title="RP-1">\n        kerosene\n       </a>\n       -fueled booster stage, each equipped with airbreathing jet engines for powered return to a runway at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       launch site. Other components of the system included a permanent modular space station, reusable\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_tug" title="Space tug">\n        space tug\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/NERVA" title="NERVA">\n        nuclear\n       </a>\n       interplanetary ferry, leading to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_mission_to_Mars" title="Human mission to Mars">\n        human expedition to Mars\n       </a>\n       as early as 1986, or as late as 2000, depending on the level of funding allocated. However, Nixon knew the American political climate would not support Congressional funding for such an ambition, and killed proposals for all but the Shuttle, possibly to be followed by the space station.\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Plans for the Shuttle were scaled back\n       </a>\n       to reduce development risk, cost, and time, replacing the piloted flyback booster with two reusable\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Booster">\n        solid rocket boosters\n       </a>\n       , and the smaller orbiter would use an expendable\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n        external propellant tank\n       </a>\n       to feed its hydrogen-fueled\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_main_engine" title="Space Shuttle main engine">\n        main engines\n       </a>\n       . The orbiter would have to make unpowered landings.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Atlantis_landing_at_KSC_following_STS-122_(crop).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2600" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis_landing_at_KSC_following_STS-122_%28crop%29.jpg/220px-Space_Shuttle_Atlantis_landing_at_KSC_following_STS-122_%28crop%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis_landing_at_KSC_following_STS-122_%28crop%29.jpg/330px-Space_Shuttle_Atlantis_landing_at_KSC_following_STS-122_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis_landing_at_KSC_following_STS-122_%28crop%29.jpg/440px-Space_Shuttle_Atlantis_landing_at_KSC_following_STS-122_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Atlantis_landing_at_KSC_following_STS-122_(crop).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Space Shuttle orbiter, as built\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The two nations continued to compete rather than cooperate in space, as the US turned to developing the Space Shuttle and planning the space station, dubbed\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Station_Freedom" title="Space Station Freedom">\n         Freedom\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . The USSR launched three\n       <a href="/wiki/Almaz" title="Almaz">\n        Almaz\n       </a>\n       military sortie stations from 1973 to 1977, disguised as Salyuts. They followed Salyut with the development of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">\n         Mir\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , the first modular, semi-permanent space station, the construction of which took place from 1986 to 1996.\n       <i>\n        Mir\n       </i>\n       orbited at an altitude of 354 kilometers (191 nautical miles), at a 51.6\xc2\xb0 inclination. It was occupied for 4,592 days, and made a controlled reentry in 2001.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buran_on_An-225_(Le_Bourget_1989)_(cropped).JPEG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="568" data-file-width="1076" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Buran_on_An-225_%28Le_Bourget_1989%29_%28cropped%29.JPEG/220px-Buran_on_An-225_%28Le_Bourget_1989%29_%28cropped%29.JPEG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Buran_on_An-225_%28Le_Bourget_1989%29_%28cropped%29.JPEG/330px-Buran_on_An-225_%28Le_Bourget_1989%29_%28cropped%29.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Buran_on_An-225_%28Le_Bourget_1989%29_%28cropped%29.JPEG/440px-Buran_on_An-225_%28Le_Bourget_1989%29_%28cropped%29.JPEG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buran_on_An-225_(Le_Bourget_1989)_(cropped).JPEG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Buran Orbiter 1K1 at\n         <a href="/wiki/Le_Bourget" title="Le Bourget">\n          Le Bourget\n         </a>\n         airshow, 1989\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Space Shuttle started flying in 1981, but the US Congress failed to approve sufficient funds to make\n       <i>\n        Freedom\n       </i>\n       a reality. A fleet of four shuttles was built:\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n         Columbia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">\n         Challenger\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n         Discovery\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n         Atlantis\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . A fifth shuttle,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n         Endeavour\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , was built to replace\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       , which was destroyed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        an accident during launch\n       </a>\n       that killed 7 astronauts on 28 January 1986. Twenty-two Shuttle flights carried a\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        European Space Agency\n       </a>\n       sortie space station called\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">\n        Spacelab\n       </a>\n       in the payload bay from 1983 to 1998.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StoryShuttle_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-StoryShuttle-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The USSR copied the reusable\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_orbiter" title="Space Shuttle orbiter">\n        Space Shuttle orbiter\n       </a>\n       , which it called\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Buran_programme" title="Buran programme">\n         Buran\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . It was designed to be launched into orbit by the expendable\n       <a href="/wiki/Energia" title="Energia">\n        Energia\n       </a>\n       rocket, and capable of robotic orbital flight and landing. Unlike the US Shuttle,\n       <i>\n        Buran\n       </i>\n       had no main rocket engines, but like the Shuttle used its orbital maneuvering engines to perform its final orbital insertion. A single unmanned orbital test flight was successfully made in November 1988. A second test flight was planned by 1993, but the program was cancelled due to lack of funding and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">\n        dissolution of the Soviet Union\n       </a>\n       in 1991. Two more orbiters were never completed, and the first one was destroyed in a hangar roof collapse in May 2002.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="US_/_Russian_cooperation">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="US_.2F_Russian_cooperation">\n        US / Russian cooperation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: US / Russian cooperation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2116" data-file-width="3319" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg/220px-International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg/330px-International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg/440px-International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         International Space Station, assembled in orbit by US and Russia\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The dissolution of the Soviet Union in 1991 brought an end to the Cold War and opened the door to true cooperation between the US and Russia. The Soviet Soyuz and Mir programs were taken over by the Russian Federal Space Agency, now known as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roscosmos_State_Corporation" title="Roscosmos State Corporation">\n        Roscosmos State Corporation\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shuttle-Mir_Program" title="Shuttle-Mir Program">\n        Shuttle-Mir Program\n       </a>\n       included American Space Shuttles visiting the\n       <i>\n        Mir\n       </i>\n       space station, Russian cosmonauts flying on the Shuttle, and an American astronaut flying aboard a Soyuz spacecraft for long-duration expeditions aboard\n       <i>\n        Mir\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1993, President\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">\n        Bill Clinton\n       </a>\n       secured Russia\'s cooperation in converting the planned Space Station\n       <i>\n        Freedom\n       </i>\n       into the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS). Construction of the station began in 1998. The station orbits at an altitude of 409 kilometers (221\xc2\xa0nmi) and an inclination of 51.65\xc2\xb0.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Space Shuttle was retired in 2011 after 135 orbital flights, several of which helped assemble, supply, and crew the ISS.\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was destroyed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        another accident during reentry\n       </a>\n       , which killed 7 astronauts on 1 February 2003.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="China">\n        China\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: China">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       After Russia\'s launch of Sputnik 1 in 1957, Chairman\n       <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">\n        Mao Zedong\n       </a>\n       intended to place a Chinese satellite in orbit by 1959 to celebrate the 10th anniversary of the founding of the\n       <a href="/wiki/China#People.27s_Republic_of_China_.281949.E2.80.93present.29" title="China">\n        People\'s Republic of China\n       </a>\n       (PRC),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, China did not successfully launch its first satellite until 24 April 1970. Mao and Premier\n       <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">\n        Zhou Enlai\n       </a>\n       decided on 14 July 1967, that the PRC should not be left behind, and started China\'s own human spaceflight program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first attempt, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shuguang_spacecraft" title="Shuguang spacecraft">\n        Shuguang spacecraft\n       </a>\n       copied from the US Gemini, was cancelled on 13 May 1972.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       China later designed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_(spacecraft)" title="Shenzhou (spacecraft)">\n        Shenzhou spacecraft\n       </a>\n       resembling the Russian Soyuz, and became the third nation to achieve independent human spaceflight capability by launching\n       <a href="/wiki/Yang_Liwei" title="Yang Liwei">\n        Yang Liwei\n       </a>\n       on a 21-hour flight aboard\n       <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_5" title="Shenzhou 5">\n        Shenzhou 5\n       </a>\n       on 15 October 2003. China launched the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tiangong-1" title="Tiangong-1">\n        Tiangong-1\n       </a>\n       space station on 29 September 2011, and two sortie missions to it:\n       <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_9" title="Shenzhou 9">\n        Shenzhou 9\n       </a>\n       16\xe2\x80\x9329 June 2012, with China\'s first female astronaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Liu_Yang_(astronaut)" title="Liu Yang (astronaut)">\n        Liu Yang\n       </a>\n       ; and\n       <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_10" title="Shenzhou 10">\n        Shenzhou 10\n       </a>\n       , 13\xe2\x80\x9326 June 2013. The station was retired on 21 March 2016 and remains in a 363-kilometer (196-nautical-mile), 42.77\xc2\xb0 inclination orbit.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Abandoned_programs_of_other_nations">\n        Abandoned programs of other nations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Abandoned programs of other nations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        European Space Agency\n       </a>\n       began development in 1987 of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hermes_(spacecraft)" title="Hermes (spacecraft)">\n        Hermes\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Spaceplane" title="Spaceplane">\n        spaceplane\n       </a>\n       , to be launched on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       expendable launch vehicle. The project was cancelled in 1992, when it became clear that neither cost nor performance goals could be achieved. No Hermes shuttles were ever built.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Japan began development in the 1980s of the\n       <a href="/wiki/HOPE-X" title="HOPE-X">\n        HOPE-X\n       </a>\n       experimental spaceplane, to be launched on its\n       <a href="/wiki/H-IIA" title="H-IIA">\n        H-IIA\n       </a>\n       expendable launch vehicle. A string of failures in 1998 led to funding reduction, and the project\'s cancellation in 2003.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_post-Space_Shuttle_gap">\n        United States post-Space Shuttle gap\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: United States post-Space Shuttle gap">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1996" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg/170px-Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg/255px-Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg/340px-Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The launch of Ares I prototype,\n         <a href="/wiki/Ares_I-X" title="Ares I-X">\n          Ares I-X\n         </a>\n         on 28 October 2009\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Under the Bush administration, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constellation_Program" title="Constellation Program">\n        Constellation Program\n       </a>\n       included plans for retiring the Shuttle program and replacing it with the capability for spaceflight beyond low Earth orbit. In the\n       <a href="/wiki/2011_United_States_federal_budget" title="2011 United States federal budget">\n        2011 United States federal budget\n       </a>\n       , the Obama administration cancelled Constellation for being over budget and behind schedule while not innovating and investing in critical new technologies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For beyond low earth orbit human spaceflight NASA is developing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n        Orion\n       </a>\n       spacecraft to be launched by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       . Under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        Commercial Crew Development\n       </a>\n       plan, NASA will rely on transportation services provided by the private sector to reach low earth orbit, such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_X" title="Space X">\n        Space X\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">\n        Falcon 9\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragon_V2" title="Dragon V2">\n        Dragon V2\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_Corporation" title="Sierra Nevada Corporation">\n        Sierra Nevada Corporation\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Dream_Chaser" title="Dream Chaser">\n        Dream Chaser\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">\n        Boeing\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CST-100" title="CST-100">\n        CST-100\n       </a>\n       . The period between the retirement of the shuttle in 2011 and the initial operational capability of new systems in 2017, similar to the gap between the end of\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo\n       </a>\n       in 1975 and the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n        first space shuttle flight\n       </a>\n       in 1981, is referred to by a presidential Blue Ribbon Committee as the U.S. human spaceflight gap.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_private_spaceflight">\n        Commercial private spaceflight\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Commercial private spaceflight">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       After the early 2000s, a variety of\n       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">\n        private spaceflight\n       </a>\n       ventures were undertaken. Several of the companies, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Origin" title="Blue Origin">\n        Blue Origin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Galactic" title="Virgin Galactic">\n        Virgin Galactic\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_Corporation" title="Sierra Nevada Corporation">\n        Sierra Nevada\n       </a>\n       have explicit plans to advance human spaceflight. As of 2016\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , all four of those companies have development programs underway to fly commercial passengers.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A commercial\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suborbital_spaceflight" title="Suborbital spaceflight">\n        suborbital\n       </a>\n       spacecraft aimed at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">\n        space tourism\n       </a>\n       market is being developed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Galactic" title="Virgin Galactic">\n        Virgin Galactic\n       </a>\n       called\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SpaceshipTwo" title="SpaceshipTwo">\n        SpaceshipTwo\n       </a>\n       , and could reach space around 2018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Origin" title="Blue Origin">\n        Blue Origin\n       </a>\n       has begun a multi-year\n       <a href="/wiki/Flight_test" title="Flight test">\n        test\n       </a>\n       program of their\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Shepard" title="New Shepard">\n        New Shepard\n       </a>\n       vehicle and carried out six successful uncrewed test flights in 2015\xe2\x80\x932016. Blue Origin plan to fly "test passengers" in Q2 2017, and initiate commercial flights in 2018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gw20160308_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gw20160308-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars20160309_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ars20160309-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       SpaceX and\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Defense,_Space_%26_Security" title="Boeing Defense, Space &amp; Security">\n        Boeing\n       </a>\n       are both developing passenger-capable\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_spaceflight" title="Orbital spaceflight">\n        orbital\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_capsule" title="Space capsule">\n        space capsules\n       </a>\n       as of 2015, planning to fly\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        NASA astronauts to the International Space Station\n       </a>\n       by 2018. SpaceX will be carrying passengers on\n       <a href="/wiki/Dragon_2" title="Dragon 2">\n        Dragon 2\n       </a>\n       launched on a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falcon_9_full_thrust" title="Falcon 9 full thrust">\n        Falcon 9\n       </a>\n       launch vehicle. Boeing will be doing it with their\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CST-100" title="CST-100">\n        CST-100\n       </a>\n       launched on a\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Launch_Alliance" title="United Launch Alliance">\n        United Launch Alliance\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlas_V" title="Atlas V">\n        Atlas V\n       </a>\n       launch vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasaAnnounce20140906_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasaAnnounce20140906-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Development funding for these orbital-capable technologies has been provided by a mix of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_funding" title="Government funding">\n        government\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_capital" title="Private capital">\n        private\n       </a>\n       funds, with SpaceX providing a greater portion of total development funding for this human-carrying capability from private investment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20140921_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sn20140921-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASApress20140916_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASApress20140916-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There have been no public announcements of commercial offerings for orbital flights from either company, although both companies are planning some flights with their own private, not NASA, astronauts on board.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Milestones">\n        Milestones\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Milestones">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Savitskaya" title="Svetlana Savitskaya">\n        Svetlana Savitskaya\n       </a>\n       became the first woman to walk in space on 25 July 1984.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Sally_Ride" title="Sally Ride">\n        Sally Ride\n       </a>\n       became the first American woman in space in 1983.\n       <a href="/wiki/Eileen_Collins" title="Eileen Collins">\n        Eileen Collins\n       </a>\n       was the first female shuttle pilot, and with shuttle mission\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-93" title="STS-93">\n        STS-93\n       </a>\n       in 1999 she became the first woman to command a U.S. spacecraft.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The longest single human spaceflight is that of\n       <a href="/wiki/Valeri_Polyakov" title="Valeri Polyakov">\n        Valeri Polyakov\n       </a>\n       , who left Earth on 8 January 1994, and did not return until 22 March 1995 (a total of 437 days 17 h 58 min 16 s).\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergei_Krikalyov" title="Sergei Krikalyov">\n        Sergei Krikalyov\n       </a>\n       has spent the most time of anyone in space, 803 days, 9 hours, and 39 minutes altogether. The longest period of continuous human presence in space is\n       <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n        7003621500000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n       </span>\n       17\xc2\xa0years and 6\xc2\xa0days on the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       , exceeding the previous record of almost 10 years (or 3,634 days) held by\n       <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">\n        Mir\n       </a>\n       , spanning the launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-8" title="Soyuz TM-8">\n        Soyuz TM-8\n       </a>\n       on 5 September 1989 to the landing of\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-29" title="Soyuz TM-29">\n        Soyuz TM-29\n       </a>\n       on 28 August 1999.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For many years, only the USSR (later\n       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">\n        Russia\n       </a>\n       ) and the United States had their own astronauts. Citizens of other nations flew in space, beginning with the flight of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vladimir_Remek" title="Vladimir Remek">\n        Vladimir Remek\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">\n        Czech\n       </a>\n       , on a Soviet spacecraft on 2 March 1978, in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interkosmos" title="Interkosmos">\n        Interkosmos\n       </a>\n       programme. As of 2010\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , citizens from 38 nations (including\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">\n        space tourists\n       </a>\n       ) have flown in space aboard Soviet, American, Russian, and Chinese spacecraft.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_programs">\n        Space programs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Space programs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Human spaceflight programs have been conducted by the former Soviet Union and current Russian Federation, the United States, the People\'s Republic of China and by\n       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">\n        private spaceflight\n       </a>\n       company\n       <a href="/wiki/Scaled_Composites" title="Scaled Composites">\n        Scaled Composites\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="center">\n       <div class="thumb tnone">\n        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Human_spaceflight.svg">\n          <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="863" height="385" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Human_spaceflight.svg/750px-Human_spaceflight.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Human_spaceflight.svg/1125px-Human_spaceflight.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Human_spaceflight.svg/1500px-Human_spaceflight.svg.png 2x" width="750"/>\n         </a>\n         <div class="thumbcaption">\n          <div class="magnify">\n           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Human_spaceflight.svg" title="Enlarge">\n           </a>\n          </div>\n          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #204a87; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n           </span>\n           Currently have human spaceflight programs.\n          </div>\n          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #729fcf; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n           </span>\n           Confirmed and dated plans for human spaceflight programs.\n          </div>\n          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #4e9a06; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n           </span>\n           Plans for human spaceflight on the simplest form (suborbital spaceflight,\n           <i>\n            etc.\n           </i>\n           ).\n          </div>\n          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ce5c00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n           </span>\n           Plans for human spaceflight on the extreme form (space stations,\n           <i>\n            etc.\n           </i>\n           ).\n          </div>\n          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #2e3436; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n           </span>\n           Once had official plans for human spaceflight programs, but have since been abandoned.\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_programs">\n        Current programs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Current programs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_vehicle" title="Space vehicle">\n        Space vehicles\n       </a>\n       are\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">\n        spacecraft\n       </a>\n       used for transportation between the Earth\'s surface and outer space, or between locations in outer space. The following space vehicles and\n       <a href="/wiki/Spaceport" title="Spaceport">\n        spaceports\n       </a>\n       are currently used for launching human spaceflights:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_programme" title="Soyuz programme">\n         Soyuz program\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">\n         USSR\n        </a>\n        /Russia): spacecraft on\n        <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_(rocket_family)" title="Soyuz (rocket family)">\n         Soyuz launch vehicle\n        </a>\n        , from\n        <a href="/wiki/Baikonur_Cosmodrome" title="Baikonur Cosmodrome">\n         Baikonur Cosmodrome\n        </a>\n        ; 129 orbital flights since 1967, including one in-flight abort which failed to reach orbit, as of July 2016\n        <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit">\n          [update]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_program" title="Shenzhou program">\n         Shenzhou program\n        </a>\n        (Chinese): spacecraft on\n        <a href="/wiki/Long_March_(rocket_family)" title="Long March (rocket family)">\n         Long March launch vehicle\n        </a>\n        , from\n        <a href="/wiki/Jiuquan_Satellite_Launch_Center" title="Jiuquan Satellite Launch Center">\n         Jiuquan Satellite Launch Center\n        </a>\n        ; 5 flights since 2003, as of July 2016\n        <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit">\n          [update]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       The following\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_stations" title="Space stations">\n        space stations\n       </a>\n       are currently maintained in Earth orbit for human occupation:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n         International Space Station\n        </a>\n        (US and Russia) assembled in orbit: altitude 409 kilometers (221 nautical miles), 51.65\xc2\xb0 inclination; crews transported by Soyuz spacecraft\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Tiangong-2" title="Tiangong-2">\n         Tiangong-2\n        </a>\n        (Chinese): altitude 392 kilometers (212 nautical miles); crews transported by Shenzhou spacecraft\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Numerous private companies attempted human spaceflight programs in an effort to win the $10 million\n       <a href="/wiki/Ansari_X_Prize" title="Ansari X Prize">\n        Ansari X Prize\n       </a>\n       . The first private human spaceflight took place on 21 June 2004, when SpaceShipOne conducted a suborbital flight. SpaceShipOne captured the prize on 4 October 2004, when it accomplished two consecutive flights within one week.\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceShipTwo" title="SpaceShipTwo">\n        SpaceShipTwo\n       </a>\n       , launching from the carrier aircraft\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scaled_Composites_WhiteKnightTwo" title="Scaled Composites WhiteKnightTwo">\n        White Knight Two\n       </a>\n       , is planned to conduct regular suborbital space tourism.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most of the time, the only humans in space are those aboard the ISS, whose crew of six spends up to six months at a time in\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESA" title="ESA">\n        ESA\n       </a>\n       use the term "human spaceflight" to refer to their programs of launching people into space. These endeavors have also been referred to as "manned space missions," though because of gender specificity this is no longer official parlance according to NASA style guides.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Planned_future_programs">\n        Planned future programs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Planned future programs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       is developing a plan to land humans on Mars by the 2030s. The first step in this mission begins sometime during 2020, when NASA plans to send an uncrewed craft into deep space to retrieve an asteroid.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The asteroid will be pushed into the moon\xe2\x80\x99s orbit, and studied by astronauts aboard\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n        Orion\n       </a>\n       , NASA\xe2\x80\x99s first human spacecraft in a generation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Orion\xe2\x80\x99s crew will return to Earth with samples of the asteroid and their collected data. In addition to broadening America\xe2\x80\x99s space capabilities, this mission will test newly developed technology, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_electric_propulsion" title="Solar electric propulsion">\n        solar electric propulsion\n       </a>\n       , which uses solar arrays for energy and requires ten times less propellant than the conventional chemical counterpart used for powering space shuttles to orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Several other countries and space agencies have announced and begun human spaceflight programs by their own technology,\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">\n        JAXA\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">\n        Iran\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Space_Agency" title="Iranian Space Agency">\n        ISA\n       </a>\n       ) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">\n        Malaysia\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaysian_National_Space_Agency" title="Malaysian National Space Agency">\n        MNSA\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation" title="Indian Space Research Organisation">\n        Indian Space Research Organisation\n       </a>\n       (ISRO) has begun work on pre-project activities of a human space flight mission program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The objective is to carry a crew of two to Low Earth Orbit (LEO) and return them safely to a predefined destination on Earth. The program is proposed to be implemented in defined phases. Currently, the pre-project activities are progressing with a focus on the development of critical technologies for subsystems such as the Crew Module (CM), Environmental Control and Life Support System (ECLSS), Crew Escape System, etc. The department has initiated pre-project activities to study technical and managerial issues related to crewed missions. The program envisages the development of a fully autonomous orbital vehicle carrying 2 or 3 crew members to about 300\xc2\xa0km low earth orbit and their safe return.\n      </p>\n      <div class="timeline-wrapper">\n       <map id="timeline_126e6bcd878a87c2161d34bc81122893" name="timeline_126e6bcd878a87c2161d34bc81122893">\n        <area alt="Roman Romanenko" coords="762,438,798,459" href="/wiki/Roman_Romanenko" shape="rect" title="Roman Romanenko"/>\n        <area alt="Frank De Winne" coords="762,424,798,445" href="/wiki/Frank_De_Winne" shape="rect" title="Frank De Winne"/>\n        <area alt="Timothy Kopra" coords="758,409,795,430" href="/wiki/Timothy_Kopra" shape="rect" title="Timothy Kopra"/>\n        <area alt="Michael R.
