H-IIB\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_concerns">\n        Safety concerns\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Safety concerns">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       There are two main sources of hazard in space flight: those due to the\n       <i>\n        environment\n       </i>\n       of space which make it hostile to the human body, and the potential for\n       <i>\n        mechanical\n       </i>\n       malfunctions of the equipment required to accomplish space flight.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_hazards">\n        Environmental hazards\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Environmental hazards">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_habitat" title="Space habitat">\n        Space habitat\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body" title="Effect of spaceflight on the human body">\n        Effect of spaceflight on the human body\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Locomotion_in_Space" title="Locomotion in Space">\n        Locomotion in Space\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Planners of human spaceflight missions face a number of safety concerns.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Life_support">\n        Life support\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Life support">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Life_support_system" title="Life support system">\n        Life support system\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The immediate needs for breathable air and drinkable water are addressed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Life_support_system" title="Life support system">\n        life support system\n       </a>\n       of the spacecraft.\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronautical_hygiene" title="Astronautical hygiene">\n        Astronautical hygiene\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_issues">\n        Medical issues\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Medical issues">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body" title="Effect of spaceflight on the human body">\n        Effect of spaceflight on the human body\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_medicine" title="Space medicine">\n        Space medicine\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Medical consequences such as possible\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blindness" title="Blindness">\n        blindness\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bone_Loss" title="Bone Loss">\n        bone loss\n       </a>\n       have been associated with human\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_flight" title="Space flight">\n        space flight\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20140127_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140127-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired-20120723_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wired-20120723-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 31 December 2012, a\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       -supported study reported that spaceflight may harm the\n       <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">\n        brain\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronauts" title="Astronauts">\n        astronauts\n       </a>\n       and accelerate the onset of\n       <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer\'s disease">\n        Alzheimer\'s disease\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PLOS-20121231_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PLOS-20121231-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpaceRef-20130101_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SpaceRef-20130101-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NasaWatch-20130103_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NasaWatch-20130103-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In October 2015, the\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Office_of_Inspector_General" title="NASA Office of Inspector General">\n        NASA Office of Inspector General\n       </a>\n       issued a\n       <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body" title="Effect of spaceflight on the human body">\n        health hazards report\n       </a>\n       related to\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">\n        space exploration\n       </a>\n       , including a\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_mission_to_Mars" title="Human mission to Mars">\n        human mission to Mars\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20151029_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP-20151029-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20151029oig_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20151029oig-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 2 November 2017, scientists reported that significant changes in the position and structure of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">\n        brain\n       </a>\n       have been found in\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">\n        astronauts\n       </a>\n       who have taken\n       <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body" title="Effect of spaceflight on the human body">\n        trips in space\n       </a>\n       , based on\n       <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_resonance_imaging" title="Magnetic resonance imaging">\n        MRI studies\n       </a>\n       . Astronauts who took longer space trips were associated with greater brain changes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEJM-20171102_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NEJM-20171102-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QTZ-20171103_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-QTZ-20171103-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h5>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Microgravity">\n        Microgravity\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Microgravity">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h5>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Weightlessness" title="Weightlessness">\n        Weightlessness\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_fluid_shift.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="151" data-file-width="293" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Space_fluid_shift.gif/220px-Space_fluid_shift.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/50/Space_fluid_shift.gif 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_fluid_shift.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The effects of microgravity on fluid distribution around the body (greatly exaggerated).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Medical data from astronauts in low earth orbits for long periods, dating back to the 1970s, show several adverse effects of a microgravity environment: loss of\n       <a href="/wiki/Bone" title="Bone">\n        bone\n       </a>\n       density, decreased muscle strength and endurance, postural instability, and reductions in aerobic capacity. Over time these\n       <a href="/wiki/Deconditioning" title="Deconditioning">\n        deconditioning\n       </a>\n       effects can impair astronauts\xe2\x80\x99 performance or increase their risk of injury.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In a weightless environment, astronauts put almost no weight on the back\n       <a href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">\n        muscles\n       </a>\n       or leg muscles used for standing up, which causes them to weaken and get smaller. Astronauts can lose up to twenty per cent of their muscle mass on spaceflights lasting five to eleven days. The consequent loss of strength could be a serious problem in case of a landing emergency.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Upon return to Earth from long-duration flights, astronauts are considerably weakened, and are not allowed to drive a car for twenty-one days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Astronauts experiencing weightlessness will often lose their orientation, get\n       <a href="/wiki/Motion_sickness" title="Motion sickness">\n        motion sickness\n       </a>\n       , and lose their sense of direction as their bodies try to get used to a weightless environment. When they get back to Earth, or any other mass with gravity, they have to readjust to the gravity and may have problems standing up, focusing their gaze, walking and turning. Importantly, those body motor disturbances after changing from different gravities only get worse the longer the exposure to little gravity.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       These changes will affect operational activities including approach and landing, docking, remote manipulation, and emergencies that may happen while landing. This can be a major roadblock to mission success.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition, after long\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_flight" title="Space flight">\n        space flight\n       </a>\n       missions, male astronauts may experience severe\n       <a href="/wiki/Visual_system" title="Visual system">\n        eyesight\n       </a>\n       problems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mader-2011_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mader-2011-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puiu-20111109_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Puiu-20111109-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN-20120109_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CNN-20120109-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space-20120313_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Space-20120313-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radiology-20120313_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Radiology-20120313-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Such eyesight problems may be a major concern for future deep space flight missions, including a\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Crewed_mission&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Crewed mission (page does not exist)">\n        crewed mission\n       </a>\n       to the planet\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mader-2011_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mader-2011-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puiu-20111109_45-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Puiu-20111109-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN-20120109_46-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CNN-20120109-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space-20120313_47-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Space-20120313-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WIRED-20140212_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WIRED-20140212-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h5>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radiation">\n        Radiation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Radiation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h5>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Health_threat_from_cosmic_rays" title="Health threat from cosmic rays">\n        Health threat from cosmic rays\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1017" data-file-width="900" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/220px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/330px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/440px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Comparison of Radiation Doses \xe2\x80\x93 includes the amount detected on the trip from Earth to Mars by the\n         <a href="/wiki/Radiation_assessment_detector" title="Radiation assessment detector">\n          RAD\n         </a>\n         on the\n         <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">\n          MSL\n         </a>\n         (2011\xe2\x80\x932013).\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531a_50-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531a-50">\n           [50]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Without proper shielding, the crews of missions beyond low Earth orbit (LEO) might be at risk from high-energy protons emitted by\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_flare" title="Solar flare">\n        solar flares\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Townsend" title="Lawrence Townsend">\n        Lawrence Townsend\n       </a>\n       of the University of Tennessee and others have studied\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_storm_of_1859" title="Solar storm of 1859">\n        the most powerful solar flare ever recorded\n       </a>\n       . That flare was seen by the British astronomer\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Christopher_Carrington" title="Richard Christopher Carrington">\n        Richard Carrington\n       </a>\n       in September 1859. Radiation doses astronauts would receive from a Carrington-type flare could cause acute radiation sickness and possibly even death.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another type of radiation,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galactic_cosmic_ray" title="Galactic cosmic ray">\n        galactic cosmic rays\n       </a>\n       , presents further challenges to human spaceflight beyond low Earth orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is also some scientific concern that extended spaceflight might slow down the body\xe2\x80\x99s ability to protect itself against diseases.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some of the problems are a weakened\n       <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">\n        immune system\n       </a>\n       and the activation of dormant\n       <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">\n        viruses\n       </a>\n       in the body.\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n        Radiation\n       </a>\n       can cause both short and long term consequences to the bone marrow stem cells which create the blood and immune systems. Because the interior of a spacecraft is so small, a weakened immune system and more active viruses in the body can lead to a fast spread of infection.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h5>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Isolation">\n        Isolation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Isolation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h5>\n      <p>\n       During long missions, astronauts are isolated and confined into small spaces.\n       <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">\n        Depression\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cabin_fever" title="Cabin fever">\n        cabin fever\n       </a>\n       and other psychological problems may impact the crew\'s safety and mission success.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Astronauts may not be able to quickly return to Earth or receive medical supplies, equipment or personnel if a medical emergency occurs. The astronauts may have to rely for long periods on their limited existing resources and medical advice from the ground.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mechanical_hazards">\n        Mechanical hazards\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Mechanical hazards">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Space flight requires much higher velocities than ground or air transportation, which in turn requires the use of high\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy_density" title="Energy density">\n        energy density\n       </a>\n       propellants for launch, and the dissipation of large amounts of energy, usually as heat, for safe reentry through the Earth\'s atmosphere.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch">\n        Launch\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Launch">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_escape_system" title="Launch escape system">\n        Launch escape system\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since rockets carry the potential for fire or explosive destruction,\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_capsule" title="Space capsule">\n        space capsules\n       </a>\n       generally employ some sort of\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_escape_system" title="Launch escape system">\n        launch escape system\n       </a>\n       , consisting either of a tower-mounted solid fuel rocket to quickly carry the capsule away from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">\n        launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       (employed on\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Mercury" title="Project Mercury">\n        Mercury\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_(spacecraft)" title="Apollo (spacecraft)">\n        Apollo\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">\n        Soyuz\n       </a>\n       ), or else\n       <a href="/wiki/Ejection_seat" title="Ejection seat">\n        ejection seats\n       </a>\n       (employed on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vostok_spacecraft" title="Vostok spacecraft">\n        Vostok\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Gemini" title="Project Gemini">\n        Gemini\n       </a>\n       ) to carry astronauts out of the capsule and away for individual parachute landing. The escape tower is discarded at some point before the launch is complete, at a point where an abort can be performed using the spacecraft\'s engines.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Such a system is not always practical for multiple crew member vehicles (particularly\n       <a href="/wiki/Spaceplane" title="Spaceplane">\n        spaceplanes\n       </a>\n       ), depending on location of egress hatch(es). When the single-hatch Vostok capsule was modified to become the 2 or 3-person\n       <a href="/wiki/Voskhod_(spacecraft)" title="Voskhod (spacecraft)">\n        Voskhod\n       </a>\n       , the single-cosmonaut ejection seat could not be used, and no escape tower system was added. The two Voskhod flights in 1964 and 1965 avoided launch mishaps. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       carried ejection seats and escape hatches for its pilot and copilot in early flights, but these could not be used for passengers who sat below the flight deck on later flights, and so were discontinued.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The only in-flight launch abort of a crewed flight occurred on\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_7K-T_No.39" title="Soyuz 7K-T No.39">\n        Soyuz 18a\n       </a>\n       on 5 April 1975. The abort occurred after the launch escape system had been jettisoned, when the launch vehicle\'s spent second stage failed to separate before the third stage ignited. The vehicle strayed off course, and the crew separated the spacecraft and fired its engines to pull it away from the errant rocket. Both cosmonauts landed safely.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the only use of a launch escape system on a crewed flight, the planned\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_7K-ST_No._16L" title="Soyuz 7K-ST No. 16L">\n        Soyuz T-10a\n       </a>\n       launch on 26 September 1983 was aborted by a launch vehicle fire 90 seconds before liftoff. Both cosmonauts aboard landed safely.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The only crew fatality during launch occurred on 28 January 1986, when the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Challenger\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       broke apart 73 seconds after liftoff, due to failure of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Booster">\n        solid rocket booster\n       </a>\n       seal which caused separation of the booster and failure of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n        external fuel tank\n       </a>\n       , resulting in explosion of the fuel. All seven crew members were killed.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reentry_and_landing">\n        Reentry and landing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Reentry and landing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_reentry" title="Atmospheric reentry">\n        Atmospheric reentry\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The single pilot of\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_1" title="Soyuz 1">\n        Soyuz 1\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Komarov" title="Vladimir Komarov">\n        Vladimir Komarov\n       </a>\n       was killed when his capsule\'s parachutes failed during an emergency landing on 24 April 1967, causing the capsule to crash.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The crew of seven aboard the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       were killed on reentry after completing a\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n        successful mission in space\n       </a>\n       on 1 February 2003. A wing leading edge\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reinforced_carbon-carbon" title="Reinforced carbon-carbon">\n        reinforced carbon-carbon\n       </a>\n       heat shield had been damaged by a piece of frozen external tank foam insulation which broke off and struck the wing during launch. Hot reentry gasses entered and destroyed the wing structure, leading to breakup of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_orbiter" title="Space Shuttle orbiter">\n        orbiter vehicle\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Artificial_atmosphere">\n        Artificial atmosphere\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Artificial atmosphere">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       There are two basic choices for an artificial atmosphere: either an Earth-like mixture of oxygen in an inert gas such as nitrogen or helium, or pure oxygen, which can be used at lower than standard atmospheric pressure. A nitrogen-oxygen mixture is used in the International Space Station and Soyuz spacecraft, while low-pressure pure oxygen is commonly used in space suits for\n       <a href="/wiki/Extravehicular_activity" title="Extravehicular activity">\n        extravehicular activity\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Use of a gas mixture carries risk of\n       <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">\n        decompression sickness\n       </a>\n       (commonly known as "the bends") when transitioning to or from the pure oxygen space suit environment. There have also been instances of injury and fatalities caused by suffocation in the presence of too much nitrogen and not enough oxygen.\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        In 1960,\n        <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Aircraft" title="McDonnell Aircraft">\n         McDonnell Aircraft\n        </a>\n        test pilot G.B. North passed out and was seriously injured when testing a Mercury cabin / spacesuit atmosphere system in a vacuum chamber, due to nitrogen-rich air leaking from the cabin into his space suit feed.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n         <a href="#cite_note-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        This incident led NASA to decide on a pure oxygen atmosphere for the Mercury, Gemini, and Apollo spacecraft.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        In 1981, three pad workers were killed by a nitrogen-rich atmosphere in the aft engine compartment of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n         Space Shuttle\n         <i>\n          Columbia\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        at the\n        <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n         Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n         <a href="#cite_note-56">\n          [56]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        In 1995, two pad workers were similarly killed by a nitrogen leak in a confined area of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n         Ariane 5\n        </a>\n        launch pad at\n        <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">\n         Guiana Space Centre\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n         <a href="#cite_note-57">\n          [57]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       A pure oxygen atmosphere carries risk of fire. The original design of the Apollo spacecraft used pure oxygen at greater than atmospheric pressure prior to launch. An electrical fire started in the cabin of\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_1" title="Apollo 1">\n        Apollo 1\n       </a>\n       during a ground test at\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station_Launch_Complex_34" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station Launch Complex 34">\n        Cape Kennedy Air Force Station Launch Complex 34\n       </a>\n       on 27 January 1967, and spread rapidly. The high pressure (increased even higher by the fire) prevented removal of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Plug_door" title="Plug door">\n        plug door\n       </a>\n       hatch cover in time to rescue the crew. All three,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gus_Grissom" title="Gus Grissom">\n        Gus Grissom\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_H._White" title="Edward H. White">\n        Edward H. White\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roger_Chaffee" title="Roger Chaffee">\n        Roger Chaffee\n       </a>\n       , were killed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP4029_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SP4029-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This led NASA to use a nitrogen/oxygen atmosphere before launch, and low pressure pure oxygen only in space.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reliability">\n        Reliability\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Reliability">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Reliability_engineering" title="Reliability engineering">\n        Reliability engineering\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The March 1966\n       <a href="/wiki/Gemini_8" title="Gemini 8">\n        Gemini 8\n       </a>\n       mission was aborted in orbit when an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attitude_control_system" title="Attitude control system">\n        attitude control system\n       </a>\n       thruster stuck in the on position, sending the craft into a dangerous spin which threatened the lives of\n       <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">\n        Neil Armstrong\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Scott" title="David Scott">\n        David Scott\n       </a>\n       . Armstrong had to shut the control system off and use the reentry control system to stop the spin. The craft made an emergency reentry and the astronauts landed safely. The most probable cause was determined to be an electrical short due to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Static_electricity" title="Static electricity">\n        static electricity\n       </a>\n       discharge, which caused the thruster to remain powered even when switched off. The control system was modified to put each thruster on its own isolated circuit.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The third lunar landing expedition\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">\n        Apollo 13\n       </a>\n       in April 1970, was aborted and the lives of the crew,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Lovell" title="Jim Lovell">\n        James Lovell\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jack_Swigert" title="Jack Swigert">\n        Jack Swigert\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fred_Haise" title="Fred Haise">\n        Fred Haise\n       </a>\n       , were threatened by failure of a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cryogenic" title="Cryogenic">\n        cryogenic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Liquid_oxygen" title="Liquid oxygen">\n        liquid oxygen\n       </a>\n       tank en route to the Moon. The tank burst when electrical power was applied to internal stirring fans in the tank, causing the immediate loss of all of its contents, and also damaging the second tank, causing the loss of its remaining oxygen in a span of 130 minutes. This in turn caused loss of electrical power provided by\n       <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">\n        fuel cells\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">\n        command spacecraft\n       </a>\n       . The crew managed to return to Earth safely by using the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module" title="Apollo Lunar Module">\n        lunar landing craft\n       </a>\n       as a "life boat". The tank failure was determined to be caused by two mistakes. The tank\'s drain fitting had been damaged when it was dropped during factory testing. This necessitated use of its internal heaters to boil out the oxygen after a pre-launch test, which in turn damaged the fan wiring\'s electrical insulation, because the thermostats on the heaters did not meet the required voltage rating due to a vendor miscommunication.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fatality_risk">\n        Fatality risk\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Fatality risk">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_spaceflight-related_accidents_and_incidents#Non-astronaut_fatalities" title="List of spaceflight-related accidents and incidents">\n        List of spaceflight-related accidents and incidents \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Non-astronaut fatalities\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As of December 2015\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , 22 crew members have died in accidents aboard spacecraft. Over 100 others have died in accidents during activity directly related to spaceflight or testing.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Date\n gases to penetrate casing and burn through a strut connecting booster to the\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n          External Tank\n class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_spaceflight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <ol class="references">\n        <li id="cite_note-1">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-1">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation web">\n           <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20101221004158/http://www.nasa.gov/news/budget/index.html" rel="nofollow">\n            "FY 2011
